## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task seeks a constitutive relationship σ(ε, T) connecting stress to strain and temperature, a fundamental problem in materials science where temperature-dependent elastic/plastic behavior must be captured.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) (linear elasticity with T-dependent modulus)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - c1 * T) (modulus decreasing linearly with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear plastic stress-strain, Ramberg-Osgood type)
- Johnson-Cook strain hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal term)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (1 - c2 * T) (saturating hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Ludwik with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (Ludwik model with exponential thermal factor)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive law)
- Zerilli-Armstrong type: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T + c3 * T * epsilon) (thermally activated dislocation model)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo/sinh creep law rearranged)
- Arrhenius-type constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (1 / T)) (thermally activated deformation with inverse-T dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening at high T → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T**n) or exp(-c*T) reducing stress magnitude
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating dislocation density saturation
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**n with 0 < n < 1 reflecting work hardening in metals
- Thermally activated processes → exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) terms reflecting Arrhenius-type thermal activation of dislocation motion
- Yield stress offset → additive constant c0 representing initial yield strength independent of strain
- Temperature-dependent modulus → multiplicative coupling between epsilon and a function of T, since elastic modulus varies with temperature
- Strain-temperature coupling → product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 reflecting interaction between thermal and mechanical effects
- Phase transition or regime change → abrupt change in σ(T) slope at critical temperature, possibly captured by tanh-based smooth transitions
